Basic Rules of Agency for Purchase
Basic rules for agents in buying and selling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fundamental rules of agency for purchase and identify when a purchase belongs to the principal or to the agent.

Core Idea
An agent cannot buy a specified item for himself; the purchase binds the principal unless the agent violates the terms.

This lesson introduces the core principles of agency for purchase from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. You will learn when an agent's purchase is valid for the principal and when it defaults to the agent. The text distinguishes between specific and non-specific items, and between different payment methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of agency
Determine whether the agent was appointed to buy a specific item or a non-specific item. The ruling differs based on this.
For a specific item, the agent cannot buy for himself.
2
Check the price and payment
Examine whether the agent used the specified currency and price. If he used a different currency or a higher price, the purchase is for the agent.
A lower price is acceptable if it benefits the principal.
3
Examine the agent's intention
If the item is non-specific, the purchase is for the agent unless he explicitly intends for the principal or uses the principal's money.
Intention can be expressed at the time of purchase.
4
Apply the ruling on self-dismissal
If the agent buys for himself in the principal's presence, it is valid; in the principal's absence, it is not.
This is based on the principle of not harming the principal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء لا يشتريه لنفسه، فلو اشتراه بغير النقود، أو بخلاف ما سمى له من الثمن، وقع أي الوكيل أي الموكل للوكيل، وإن كان بغير عينه، فالشراء للوكيل، إلا أن ينوي للموكل أو يشتريه بماله، فاشتراه أي ينصرف إليه أي الوكيل لأن في الشراء عزل نفسه عن الوكالة، وهو لا يملك عزل نفسه إلا بحضرة الموكل وهذا إذا كان الموكل غائباً، حتى لو كان حاضراً، وصرح الوكيل بأنه يشتريه لنفسه كان المشترى له؛ لأن له أن يعزل نفسه بحضرة الموكل، وليس له ذلك بغير علمه؛ لأن فيه تعزيرا له بخلاف ما إذا وكله أن يزوجه امرأة معينة، حيث جاز له أن يتزوج بها؛ لأن النكاح الذي أتى به الوكيل غير داخل تحت أمره؛ لأن الداخل تحت الوكالة نكاح مضاف إلى الموكل، فكان مخالفاً بإضافته إلى نفسه، فانعزل في ضمن المخالفة، وفي الوكالة بالشراء الداخل فيها شراء مطلق غير مقيد بالإضافة إلى أحد، فكل شيء أتى به لا يكون مخالفاً، نعم، لو خالف مقتضى كلام الأمر في جنس الثمن أو قدره كان مخالفا، ولو وكله رجل آخر بأن يشتري له ذلك الشيء بعينه فاشتراه له كان للموكل الأول دون الثاني؛ لأنه إذا لم يملك الشراء لنفسه، فالأولى أن لا يملك الشراء لغيره. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧٢/٢] يشتريه لنفسه: لأنه غرر فلو اشتراه لنفسه فهو للأمر. (ط، عيني) فلو اشتراه بغير النقود إلخ : [ بأن اشتراه بالعروض أو بالحيوان] وقد أمره الموكل بالشراء بالنقود، وقوله: "أو بخلاف ما سمى له من الثمن" إن كان أزيد من المسمى، فإن اشتراه بأقل من المسمى بأن وكله بالشراء بمائة، فاشتراه بتسعين، نفذ على الآمر ؛ لأنه خلاف إلى خير، غير أنه إذا اختلف الجنس بأن أمره بالدراهم واشترى مخالفاً مطلقاً، ولو إلى خير، ولا فرق في هذا بين أن يكون وكيلاً بالشراء أو بالبيع، وقوله: "وقع بالدنانير، يصير للوكيل"؛ لأنه خالف أمره في الصورتين فينفذ العقد عليه، وينعزل في ضمن المخالفة. (عيني، فتح) بغير عينه إلخ: أي إذا وكله بشراء عبد بغير عينه مثلا، فاشترى عبداً ، فهو للوكيل إلا أن يقول وقت الشراء: نويت الشراء للموكل أو يشتريه بمال الموكل، والمسألة على وجوه، وسيأتي تفصيله [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٦٣/٥] (عناية) بماله المراد من قول المصنف ويشتريه بماله أن يضيف العقد إلى مال الموكل سواء نقد الثمن من ماله أو من مال غيره، وإنما قيد به؛ لأنه لو أضاف العقد إلى دراهم نفسه فهو له وإن أضاف إلى دراهم مطلقة، فإن نواها للأمر، فهو كما نوى وإن نواها لنفسه فهو له. والحاصل أنه لا يخلو إما أن يضيف العقد إلى مال الموكل أو إلى مال نفسه أو إلى دراهم مطلقة، فإن كان الأول كان للأمر، حملاً لحال الوكيل على ما لا يحل له شرعاً؛ إذ الشراء لنفسه بإضافة العقد إلى دراهم غيره مستنكر شرعاً وعرفاً؛ لكونه غصباً لدراهم الأمر، وإن كان الثاني كان للمأمور ، حملاً لفعله على ما يفعله الناس عادة؛ لجريانها بوقوع الشراء لصاحب الدراهم، وإن كان الثالث فيرجع إلى نيته، فإن نواها عند شرائه للأمر، فهو للآمر، وإن نواها لنفسه، فلنفسه؛ لأن له أن يعمل لنفسه، ويعمل للآمر في حالة التوكيل، ويكون من النقد مال من كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء وإن قال: اشتريت للآمر وقال الآمر : لنفسك، فالقول للأمر، وإن كان دفع إليه أي المأمور بهذا العبد وهو الموكل الثمن فللمأمور ، وإن قال: بعني هذا لفلان ،فباعه ثم أنكر الآمر رجل لآخر أي بع لأجلي العبد مثلاً أي فباع العبد منه أي المشتري ، أي الموكل الوكيل - الموكل عاصياً فيما إذا نواه لنفسه، وإن تكاذبا في النية بحكم النقد إجماعاً، يعني إن نقد الثمن من ماله فهو له، مال الموكل، فهو للموكل وإن تصادقا على أنه لم تحضره النية، فعند أبي يوسف: يحكم النقد كما في التكاذب، وعند محمد هو للوكيل. (عيني وفتح وعناية) لنفسك: أي اشتريت لنفسك و لم يدفع الثمن إلى المأمور. (عيني، مسكين) فالقول للأمر: أي إن لم يكن الثمن مدفوعاً إلى الوكيل إلا في وجه للشافعي ورواية عن أحمد: أن القول للمأمور، وقوله: "وإن كان دفع إليه الثمن، فللمأمور" أي إجماعاً، وهذه المسألة على ثمانية أوجه، والمذكور في المتن أحدها؛ لأنه إما أن يكون الوكيل مأمورا بشراء عبد بعينه أو بغير عينه، وكل وجه على وجهين: إما أن يكون الثمن منقوداً أو غير منقود، وكل وجه على وجهين أيضاً إما أن يكون العبد حياً حين أخبر الوكيل بالشراء أو ميتاً، فإن كان مأموراً بشراء عبد بعينه، فإن أخبر عن شرائه، والعبد حي قائم، فالقول للمأمور إجماعاً؛ لأنه أخبر عما يملك استئنافه ولا تهمة فيه؛ لأن الوكيل بشراء شيء بعينه لا يملك شرائه لنفسه بمثل ذلك الثمن في حال غيبته منقوداً كان الثمن أو غير منقود. وإن كان ميتاً حين أخبر فقال: هلك عندي بعد الشراء، فأنكره الموكل فإن كان الثمن غير منقود فالقول للآمر ؛ لأنه أخبر عما لا يملك استئنافه؛ لأن البيت ليس محلا لإنشاء العقد فيه، وغرضه الرجوع بالثمن، والأمر منكر، فكان القول قوله، وإن كان الثمن منقوداً فالقول للمأمور مع يمينه بالإجماع؛ لأن الثمن كان أمانة في يده، وقد ادعى الخروج عن عهدة الأمانة من وجه الذي أمر به، وإن كان العبد بغير عينه، فإن كان حياً، فقال المأمور: اشتريته لك، وقال الآمر : لا بل اشتريته لنفسك، فإن كان الثمن منقوداً، فالقول للمأمور، وإن لم يكن الثمن منقوداً، فالقول للآمر عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا للمأمور. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧٢/٢] وإن كان العبد ميتا مسألة الكتاب فإن لم يكن الثمن منقوداً فالقول للأمر، وإن كان الثمن منقوداً فالقول وهي للمأمور بالاتفاق والحاصل أن الوجه الواحد من الثمانية على الاختلاف والبواقي على الوفاق، والخلافية هي ما لو كان العبد المأمور بشرائه بغير عينه حيا ولم يكن الثمن منقودا، وعلم من تفصيل هذه المسائل أن الثمن إن كان منقودا فالقول للمأمور في جميع الصور، وإن كان غير منقود ينظر فإن كان الوكيل لا يملك إنشاء العقد بأن كان ميتا فالقول للآخر، وإن كان يملك الإنشاء فالقول للمأمور، وعندهما وكذا عند أبي حنيفة في غير موضع التهمة، وفي موضع التهمة القول للآمر (فتح) فللمأمور أي فالقول للمأمور بالإجماع أنكر الآمر: يعني أنكر أن يكون فلان أمره بذلك وقال فلان أنا أمرته. (ط، عيني)
The Book of Agency. Chapter on Agency for Sale and Purchase. He (the agent) shall not buy it for himself. So if he buys it with other than cash, or contrary to the price specified by the principal, it falls (i.e., the purchase is for the agent). And if it is non-specific (i.e., the item is not specified), the purchase is for the agent, unless he intends for the principal or buys it with the principal's money. ... And if he says, 'I bought for the principal' and the principal says, 'You bought for yourself,' the statement is for the principal. And if the price was paid to the agent, the statement is for the agent. ...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the core rulings on agency for purchase. The first ruling: an agent appointed to buy a specific item cannot buy it for himself; if he does, the purchase goes to the principal. The exception is when the agent uses a different currency or a different price than instructed—in that case the purchase is for the agent, because he has violated the terms. For non-specific items, the purchase is for the agent unless he explicitly intends the principal or uses the principal's money. The text then discusses the agent's ability to dismiss himself (cash himself) by buying for himself: this is only allowed in the presence of the principal; in the principal's absence, he cannot. A comparison is made to marriage agency. The passage continues with the case of two principals and the dispute between agent and principal about whom the purchase was for. An extensive eight-case analysis is provided, detailing when the agent's word or the principal's word is accepted based on whether the item was specific, the price was paid, and the item is still alive or dead. The Hanafi position is that the principal's word is taken unless the price was paid to the agent, in which case the agent's word is taken. The Shafi'i school and a narration from Ahmad hold the opposite in some cases. The text also covers the ruling when the agent and principal agree that the agent had no intention at the time of purchase—then the payment of the price determines ownership according to Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad holds that the agent owns it.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): The agent appointed by the principal to carry out a specific transaction.
الموكل (al-muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
الثمن المنقود (al-thaman al-manqud): The price that has actually been paid (cash) by the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an agent appointed to buy a specific item buys it for himself using the specified price, who owns the item?
A) The agent
B) The principal
C) The contract is void
D) It depends on the agent's intention

Key Takeaway
An agent cannot buy a specified item for himself; the purchase always goes to the principal unless the agent violates the terms of agency.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Resolving Disputes Between Agent and Principal: The Eight Cases
Eight-case analysis of disputes in agency for purchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the eight-case scenario for disputes between agent and principal and determine whose word is accepted in each case according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In disputes, whose word is accepted depends on three factors: whether the item was specific, whether the price was paid, and whether the item is alive or dead.

This lesson delves into the detailed eight-case analysis from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding disputes when the agent claims to have bought for the principal and the principal denies. The ruling is not uniform; it shifts based on the specificity of the item, payment status, and the condition of the item. The Hanafi position differs from other schools in some cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three axes
The eight cases are built on three binary factors: (1) specific vs non-specific item, (2) price paid (manqud) vs not paid, (3) item alive vs dead at the time of reporting.
These factors determine the authority of the agent's claim.
2
Apply the default rule
In general, if the price has been paid, the agent's word is taken (because he is trusted with the money). If not paid, the principal's word is taken.
This is subject to exceptions.
3
Consider the specific item cases
For a specific item: if alive, the agent's word is taken by consensus; if dead and price paid, agent's word; if dead and price not paid, principal's word.
The agent cannot buy a specific item for himself, so he is not suspected.
4
Consider the non-specific item cases
For a non-specific item: if alive and price paid, agent's word (consensus); if alive and price not paid, there is ikhtilaf (Abu Hanifa says principal, Sahibayn say agent); if dead and price paid, agent's word; if dead and price not paid, principal's word.
This is the only case of ikhtilaf among the eight.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
In the disputed case (non-specific, alive, price not paid), the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that the principal's word is taken, and this is the relied-upon position.
The Sahibayn's view is considered weaker.

كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء لا يشتريه لنفسه، فلو اشتراه بغير النقود، أو بخلاف ما سمى له من الثمن، وقع أي الوكيل أي الموكل للوكيل، وإن كان بغير عينه، فالشراء للوكيل، إلا أن ينوي للموكل أو يشتريه بماله، فاشتراه أي ينصرف إليه أي الوكيل لأن في الشراء عزل نفسه عن الوكالة، وهو لا يملك عزل نفسه إلا بحضرة الموكل وهذا إذا كان الموكل غائباً، حتى لو كان حاضراً، وصرح الوكيل بأنه يشتريه لنفسه كان المشترى له؛ لأن له أن يعزل نفسه بحضرة الموكل، وليس له ذلك بغير علمه؛ لأن فيه تعزيرا له بخلاف ما إذا وكله أن يزوجه امرأة معينة، حيث جاز له أن يتزوج بها؛ لأن النكاح الذي أتى به الوكيل غير داخل تحت أمره؛ لأن الداخل تحت الوكالة نكاح مضاف إلى الموكل، فكان مخالفاً بإضافته إلى نفسه، فانعزل في ضمن المخالفة، وفي الوكالة بالشراء الداخل فيها شراء مطلق غير مقيد بالإضافة إلى أحد، فكل شيء أتى به لا يكون مخالفاً، نعم، لو خالف مقتضى كلام الأمر في جنس الثمن أو قدره كان مخالفا، ولو وكله رجل آخر بأن يشتري له ذلك الشيء بعينه فاشتراه له كان للموكل الأول دون الثاني؛ لأنه إذا لم يملك الشراء لنفسه، فالأولى أن لا يملك الشراء لغيره. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧٢/٢] يشتريه لنفسه: لأنه غرر فلو اشتراه لنفسه فهو للأمر. (ط، عيني) فلو اشتراه بغير النقود إلخ : [ بأن اشتراه بالعروض أو بالحيوان] وقد أمره الموكل بالشراء بالنقود، وقوله: "أو بخلاف ما سمى له من الثمن" إن كان أزيد من المسمى، فإن اشتراه بأقل من المسمى بأن وكله بالشراء بمائة، فاشتراه بتسعين، نفذ على الآمر ؛ لأنه خلاف إلى خير، غير أنه إذا اختلف الجنس بأن أمره بالدراهم واشترى مخالفاً مطلقاً، ولو إلى خير، ولا فرق في هذا بين أن يكون وكيلاً بالشراء أو بالبيع، وقوله: "وقع بالدنانير، يصير للوكيل"؛ لأنه خالف أمره في الصورتين فينفذ العقد عليه، وينعزل في ضمن المخالفة. (عيني، فتح) بغير عينه إلخ: أي إذا وكله بشراء عبد بغير عينه مثلا، فاشترى عبداً ، فهو للوكيل إلا أن يقول وقت الشراء: نويت الشراء للموكل أو يشتريه بمال الموكل، والمسألة على وجوه، وسيأتي تفصيله [تبيين الحقائق: ٢٦٣/٥] (عناية) بماله المراد من قول المصنف ويشتريه بماله أن يضيف العقد إلى مال الموكل سواء نقد الثمن من ماله أو من مال غيره، وإنما قيد به؛ لأنه لو أضاف العقد إلى دراهم نفسه فهو له وإن أضاف إلى دراهم مطلقة، فإن نواها للأمر، فهو كما نوى وإن نواها لنفسه فهو له. والحاصل أنه لا يخلو إما أن يضيف العقد إلى مال الموكل أو إلى مال نفسه أو إلى دراهم مطلقة، فإن كان الأول كان للأمر، حملاً لحال الوكيل على ما لا يحل له شرعاً؛ إذ الشراء لنفسه بإضافة العقد إلى دراهم غيره مستنكر شرعاً وعرفاً؛ لكونه غصباً لدراهم الأمر، وإن كان الثاني كان للمأمور ، حملاً لفعله على ما يفعله الناس عادة؛ لجريانها بوقوع الشراء لصاحب الدراهم، وإن كان الثالث فيرجع إلى نيته، فإن نواها عند شرائه للأمر، فهو للآمر، وإن نواها لنفسه، فلنفسه؛ لأن له أن يعمل لنفسه، ويعمل للآمر في حالة التوكيل، ويكون من النقد مال من كتاب الوكالة باب الوكالة بالبيع والشراء وإن قال: اشتريت للآمر وقال الآمر : لنفسك، فالقول للأمر، وإن كان دفع إليه أي المأمور بهذا العبد وهو الموكل الثمن فللمأمور ، وإن قال: بعني هذا لفلان ،فباعه ثم أنكر الآمر رجل لآخر أي بع لأجلي العبد مثلاً أي فباع العبد منه أي المشتري ، أي الموكل الوكيل - الموكل عاصياً فيما إذا نواه لنفسه، وإن تكاذبا في النية بحكم النقد إجماعاً، يعني إن نقد الثمن من ماله فهو له، مال الموكل، فهو للموكل وإن تصادقا على أنه لم تحضره النية، فعند أبي يوسف: يحكم النقد كما في التكاذب، وعند محمد هو للوكيل. (عيني وفتح وعناية) لنفسك: أي اشتريت لنفسك و لم يدفع الثمن إلى المأمور. (عيني، مسكين) فالقول للأمر: أي إن لم يكن الثمن مدفوعاً إلى الوكيل إلا في وجه للشافعي ورواية عن أحمد: أن القول للمأمور، وقوله: "وإن كان دفع إليه الثمن، فللمأمور" أي إجماعاً، وهذه المسألة على ثمانية أوجه، والمذكور في المتن أحدها؛ لأنه إما أن يكون الوكيل مأمورا بشراء عبد بعينه أو بغير عينه، وكل وجه على وجهين: إما أن يكون الثمن منقوداً أو غير منقود، وكل وجه على وجهين أيضاً إما أن يكون العبد حياً حين أخبر الوكيل بالشراء أو ميتاً، فإن كان مأموراً بشراء عبد بعينه، فإن أخبر عن شرائه، والعبد حي قائم، فالقول للمأمور إجماعاً؛ لأنه أخبر عما يملك استئنافه ولا تهمة فيه؛ لأن الوكيل بشراء شيء بعينه لا يملك شرائه لنفسه بمثل ذلك الثمن في حال غيبته منقوداً كان الثمن أو غير منقود. وإن كان ميتاً حين أخبر فقال: هلك عندي بعد الشراء، فأنكره الموكل فإن كان الثمن غير منقود فالقول للآمر ؛ لأنه أخبر عما لا يملك استئنافه؛ لأن البيت ليس محلا لإنشاء العقد فيه، وغرضه الرجوع بالثمن، والأمر منكر، فكان القول قوله، وإن كان الثمن منقوداً فالقول للمأمور مع يمينه بالإجماع؛ لأن الثمن كان أمانة في يده، وقد ادعى الخروج عن عهدة الأمانة من وجه الذي أمر به، وإن كان العبد بغير عينه، فإن كان حياً، فقال المأمور: اشتريته لك، وقال الآمر : لا بل اشتريته لنفسك، فإن كان الثمن منقوداً، فالقول للمأمور، وإن لم يكن الثمن منقوداً، فالقول للآمر عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا للمأمور. [رمز الحقائق: ١٧٢/٢] وإن كان العبد ميتا مسألة الكتاب فإن لم يكن الثمن منقوداً فالقول للأمر، وإن كان الثمن منقوداً فالقول وهي للمأمور بالاتفاق والحاصل أن الوجه الواحد من الثمانية على الاختلاف والبواقي على الوفاق، والخلافية هي ما لو كان العبد المأمور بشرائه بغير عينه حيا ولم يكن الثمن منقودا، وعلم من تفصيل هذه المسائل أن الثمن إن كان منقودا فالقول للمأمور في جميع الصور، وإن كان غير منقود ينظر فإن كان الوكيل لا يملك إنشاء العقد بأن كان ميتا فالقول للآخر، وإن كان يملك الإنشاء فالقول للمأمور، وعندهما وكذا عند أبي حنيفة في غير موضع التهمة، وفي موضع التهمة القول للآمر (فتح) فللمأمور أي فالقول للمأمور بالإجماع أنكر الآمر: يعني أنكر أن يكون فلان أمره بذلك وقال فلان أنا أمرته. (ط، عيني)
The Book of Agency. Chapter on Agency for Sale and Purchase. He (the agent) shall not buy it for himself. So if he buys it with other than cash, or contrary to the price specified by the principal, it falls (i.e., the purchase is for the agent). And if it is non-specific (i.e., the item is not specified), the purchase is for the agent, unless he intends for the principal or buys it with the principal's money. ... And if he says, 'I bought for the principal' and the principal says, 'You bought for yourself,' the statement is for the principal. And if the price was paid to the agent, the statement is for the agent. ...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq lays out the core rulings on agency for purchase. The first ruling: an agent appointed to buy a specific item cannot buy it for himself; if he does, the purchase goes to the principal. The exception is when the agent uses a different currency or a different price than instructed—in that case the purchase is for the agent, because he has violated the terms. For non-specific items, the purchase is for the agent unless he explicitly intends the principal or uses the principal's money. The text then discusses the agent's ability to dismiss himself (cash himself) by buying for himself: this is only allowed in the presence of the principal; in the principal's absence, he cannot. A comparison is made to marriage agency. The passage continues with the case of two principals and the dispute between agent and principal about whom the purchase was for. An extensive eight-case analysis is provided, detailing when the agent's word or the principal's word is accepted based on whether the item was specific, the price was paid, and the item is still alive or dead. The Hanafi position is that the principal's word is taken unless the price was paid to the agent, in which case the agent's word is taken. The Shafi'i school and a narration from Ahmad hold the opposite in some cases. The text also covers the ruling when the agent and principal agree that the agent had no intention at the time of purchase—then the payment of the price determines ownership according to Abu Yusuf, while Muhammad holds that the agent owns it.

Key Terms
الوكيل (al-wakil): The agent appointed by the principal to carry out a specific transaction.
الموكل (al-muwakkil): The principal who appoints the agent.
الثمن المنقود (al-thaman al-manqud): The price that has actually been paid (cash) by the agent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent's word
B) The principal's word
C) Both are partially believed
D) The matter is referred to a judge

Key Takeaway
Only one of eight dispute scenarios is disputed: non-specific item, alive, price not paid; the Hanafi position takes the principal's word.

Eight Scenarios of Dispute Between Principal and Agent in Sale
full analysis of eight cases for agent-principal dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three factors that determine whose word is taken in an agent-principal dispute and apply them to any scenario to derive the correct ruling.

Core Idea
In agent-principal disputes, three factors—specification, payment, and life—decide whose word is taken; only one scenario is disputed among Hanafis.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentaries lays out eight distinct scenarios when an agent claims to have bought for the principal but the principal denies. The ruling on whose statement is believed (al-qawl qawl man) hinges on three variables: whether the slave was specified in the agency, whether the price was paid to the agent, and whether the slave is alive or dead at the time of the report. Understanding these factors is crucial for resolving disputes in agency transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three key variables
List the three factors that the text uses to classify the eight scenarios: specification of the item (specific vs. non-specific), payment of the price (naqdan vs. ghayr naqdan), and the status of the slave (alive vs. dead at the time of report).
These are the axes of the classification.
2
Map the eight possible combinations
Create a 2x2x2 matrix: for each combination of variables, determine whose word is taken according to the Hanafi school. Note that the text lists the ruling for each combination.
The text describes all eight, but only one is disputed.
3
Locate the disputed case
Identify the sole scenario where the Hanafi imams differ: when the slave is unspecified, alive, and the price not paid. Abu Hanifah gives the word to the principal; the Sahibayn give it to the agent.
This is the only source of ikhtilaf.
4
Understand the reasoning behind each position
Analyze the rationale: Abu Hanifah sees suspicion (tuhmah) because the agent could have bought for himself; the Sahibayn emphasize the agent's trustworthiness and the continuation of the agency.
This is a debate over the presumption of integrity vs. the likelihood of self-dealing.
5
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical fact pattern, use the three-factor framework to determine whose word is taken. For example, if the agent was told to buy any horse, paid the price, and reports he bought one that later died – then the agent's word is taken by consensus.
Practice builds mastery of the classification.

The Book of Agency. Chapter: Agency for sale and purchase. And if he said: 'I bought for the principal' and the principal said: 'for yourself', then the word is for the principal, and if he had paid the price to him, then [the word] for the agent. And if he said: 'Sell this to me for so-and-so', and he sold it, then the principal denied... [commentary] 'for yourself': meaning I bought for yourself and he did not pay the price to the agent. (Ayni, Miskin). 'The word is for the principal': meaning if the price has not been paid to the agent, except in one view of al-Shafi'i and a narration from Ahmad: that the word is for the agent. And his statement: 'And if he had paid the price to him, [the word] is for the agent' meaning by consensus. And this issue has eight aspects, and what is mentioned in the text is one of them. It is either that the agent is ordered to buy a specific slave or a non-specific one, and each aspect has two aspects: either the price is paid (naqdan) or not paid, and each aspect also has two aspects: either the slave is alive when the agent reports the purchase or dead. If he was ordered to buy a specific slave, and he reported about his purchase while the slave is alive and present, then the word is for the agent by consensus; because he reported about something he can initiate anew and there is no suspicion; because the agent to buy a specific thing cannot buy it for himself with that price in his absence, whether the price is paid or not. And if the slave was dead at the time of reporting and he said: 'He perished with me after purchase', and the principal denied, then if the price is not paid, the word is for the principal; because he reported about something he cannot initiate anew; because the house is not a place for initiating the contract, and his purpose is to recover the price, and the principal denies, so his word is taken. And if the price was paid, the word is for the agent with his oath by consensus; because the price was a trust in his hand, and he claimed discharge from the trust liability from the aspect he was ordered. And if the slave is non-specific, if he is alive, and the agent said: 'I bought it for you', and the principal said: 'No, you bought it for yourself', then if the price is paid, the word is for the agent; if the price is not paid, the word is for the principal according to Abu Hanifah, and the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] say for the agent. (Ramooz al-Haqa'iq 2:172). And if the slave is dead (the case of the book), then if the price is not paid, the word is for the principal, and if the price is paid, the word is for the agent by agreement. The summary is that one of the eight aspects is subject to difference, the rest are upon agreement. The controversial one is when the slave ordered to be purchased is non-specific, alive, and the price is not paid. And from the detail of these cases it is known that if the price is paid, the word is for the agent in all cases; if it is not paid, then: if the agent cannot initiate the contract because the slave is dead, then the word is for the other (principal); if he can initiate, then the word is for the agent according to the two, and likewise according to Abu Hanifah in a place free of suspicion, but in a place of suspicion the word is for the principal. (Fath) 'So for the agent' meaning the word is for the agent by consensus. 'The principal denied': meaning he denied that So-and-so ordered him and said: 'So-and-so, I ordered him.' (T, Ayni).
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the eight possible scenarios when an agent claims to have bought for the principal and the principal claims the agent bought for himself. The commentator (Ayni, Fath etc.) explains the base ruling from Kanz al-Daqaiq. The key factors are: (1) whether the slave was specified in the agency or not, (2) whether the price had been given to the agent (naqd) or not, and (3) whether the slave is alive or dead at the time of the report. The ruling on whose word is taken (qawl) changes with these factors. In most cases, there is consensus among the Hanafi scholars. The only point of disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifah and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is when the slave is unspecified, alive, and the price has not been paid to the agent. Imam Abu Hanifah says the principal's word is taken (because the agent could have bought for himself), while they say the agent's word is taken (because the agency is still valid). The text also notes the general principle: if the price is paid, the agent's word is always taken because the price was a trust; if not, then whether the agent can still initiate the purchase matters.

Key Terms
القول قوله (al-qawl qawluhu): The word (statement) of that person is taken as true in a dispute
الوكيل (al-wakeel): The agent who is appointed to buy or sell on behalf of another
نقد الثمن (naqd al-thaman): Payment of the price by the principal to the agent at the time of appointment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ruling When Someone Says 'Sell Me This for So-and-So' and Then Denies Agency
A ruling on the effect of iqrar and its retraction in agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a buyer's iqrar of agency and explain when the principal may take the purchased item, and when ta'ati completes the sale.

Core Idea
The buyer's iqrar binds unless the principal repudiates; ta'ati can complete the sale.

This lesson examines a common scenario in sales where a buyer declares he is purchasing as an agent but later denies the agency. The Hanafi school gives weight to the initial iqrar (admission) and only allows its repudiation by the principal's denial. Additionally, the lesson highlights that a sale can be validly concluded by mutual delivery and acceptance (ta'ati) without formal offer and acceptance, based on custom and mutual consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and the Ruling
The buyer says 'sell me this for so-and-so' indicating he is an agent. The seller sells. Later the buyer denies agency. The ruling: so-and-so (the principal) takes the slave unless he himself denies having ordered the purchase.
This is the default ruling based on iqrar.
2
Trace the Effect of Iqrar and Its Repudiation
The buyer's statement is an iqrar (admission) of agency. In Hanafi law, an iqrar is binding and not nullified by the declarant's later denial. However, it can be repudiated by the person in whose favor it is made. Thus if the principal denies, the iqrar is voided, and the buyer becomes the owner.
Only the principal's denial matters.
3
Distinguish from Fuduli Purchase
This case is not a purchase by an unauthorized agent (fuduli) because the buyer attributed the sale to himself ('sell me'), not to the principal. In fuduli, the agent says 'sell to so-and-so', and the contract is suspended until ratification.
Here the purchase is immediately effective.
4
Note the Exception: Ta'ati Sale
If the buyer delivers the slave to the principal and the principal accepts, the sale is considered concluded by ta'ati. This is valid based on custom (urf) and mutual consent (taradi), even without explicit verbal offer and acceptance or payment of price.
Ta'ati is accepted by Hanafis but not by all schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(عيني)] أي إذا قال رجل لآخر : بعني هذا العبد لأجل فلان، فإني أشتريه له وكالة عنه، فباعه البائع العبد منه، ثم أنكر المشتري أمر فلان، وقال ما كان أمرني بذلك وقال فلان أنا أمرته أخذ العبد فلان؛ لإقرار المشتري بالوكالة عنه، والإقرار بالشيء لا يبطل بالإنكار اللاحق، فيكون العبد للموكل أي لفلان وقوله : "إلا أن يقول لم آمره به" أي فحينئذ ليس لفلان أن يأخذ العبد؛ لأن إقرار المشتري ارتد برد ،فلان والإقرار مما يرتد بالرد، فينفذ على المشتري؛ لأن الشراء إذا . وجد نفاذاً ! لا يتوقف، وليس هذا من شراء الفضولي؛ لأنه أضاف البيع إلى نفسه بقوله: "بعني"، وصورة شراء الفضولي: أن يقول: بع عبدك من فلان. وقوله: "إلا أن يسلمه المشتري القائل: بعني هذا لفلان، فإن سلمه إليه، وأخذه الذي اشترى له، صار بيعاً للذي فلان، فيلزم عليه تسليم الثمن؛ لأنه صار مشترياً بالتعاطي، كالفضولي إذا اشترى الشخص ثم سلمه ودلت المسألة على أن التسليم على وجه البيع يكفي؛ لانعقاد البيع بالتعاطي، وإن لم يوجد نقد الثمن، للعرف ولوجود التراضي، وهو المعتبر في باب المعاوضات المالية. (عيني، فتح) آمره به أي بالشراء، فحينئذ لا يأخذه بل يكون للمشتري؛ لأن إقراره ارتد برد ،فلان، والإقرار مما يرتد بالرد فينفذ على المشتري (عيني) المشتري إليه أي إلى فلان فيكون لفلان التسليم، وهذا استثناء الاستثناء الأول، من وله حكم النفي، والاستثناء من النفي إثبات. (عيني)
He (the principal) takes it unless he says 'I did not order him', unless the buyer (the one who said 'sell me') delivers it to him. And if he ordered the purchase of two specific slaves and did not name a price, and he bought one of them for him, it is valid. And with their purchase for a thousand while their values are equal... (Ayni) Meaning: if a man says to another: 'Sell me this slave for the sake of so-and-so, for I am buying it for him as an agent', and the seller sells the slave to him, then the buyer denies the order of so-and-so and says 'He did not order me' and so-and-so says 'I ordered him', then so-and-so takes the slave; because the buyer's iqrar of agency for him, and an iqrar is not nullified by subsequent denial. So the slave is for the principal, i.e. so-and-so. And his statement: 'unless he says I did not order him' meaning then so-and-so has no right to take the slave; because the buyer's iqrar is repudiated by so-and-so's repudiation, and an iqrar can be repudiated, so it takes effect against the buyer. Because the purchase, when it exists, is effective and does not stop. And this is not a purchase by a fuduli (unauthorized agent); because he attributed the sale to himself by saying 'sell me'. The form of a fuduli purchase is that he says: 'Sell your slave to so-and-so.' And his statement: 'unless the buyer (the one who said 'sell me this for so-and-so') delivers it to him, and if he delivers it to him and the one for whom he bought takes it, then it becomes a sale for so-and-so, and he is obliged to pay the price; because he becomes a buyer through mutual transaction (ta'ati), like the fuduli when he buys a good and then delivers it. And the case indicates that delivery in the manner of sale suffices for the contract to be concluded by ta'ati, even if no price is paid, due to custom and the existence of mutual consent, which is considered in financial transactions. (Ayni, Fath) 'Ordered him' meaning with the purchase; then he does not take it, rather it is for the buyer; because his iqrar is repudiated by so-and-so's repudiation, and an iqrar can be repudiated, so it takes effect against the buyer. (Ayni) 'The buyer to him' meaning to so-and-so, so the delivery is for so-and-so. And this is an exception to the first exception, which has the ruling of negation, and exception from negation is affirmation. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage discusses the case where a person tells a seller: 'Sell me this slave for so-and-so; I am buying it as his agent.' After the sale, the buyer denies that so-and-so ordered him. The ruling is that so-and-so can take the slave because the buyer's declaration (iqrar) that he is acting as agent is binding. A subsequent denial does not undo the iqrar. However, if so-and-so himself denies that he appointed the buyer (saying 'I did not order him'), then the iqrar is repudiated and the buyer is stuck with the purchase (the slave remains his). There is also an exception: if the buyer delivers the slave to so-and-so and so-and-so accepts it, then the sale is considered concluded via ta'ati (mutual transaction) and so-and-so must pay the price. This is analogous to the fuduli (unauthorized agent) who buys and then delivers to the principal. The principle is that delivery with the intent of sale suffices to conclude a sale by custom and mutual consent, even without explicit offer and acceptance or payment of price.

Key Terms
إقرار (iqrar): An admission or declaration that binds the declarant; here, the buyer's statement that he is agent for so-and-so
التعاطي (al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by mutual delivery and acceptance without verbal offer and acceptance, based on custom
الفضولي (al-fuduli): An unauthorized agent who buys without prior appointment; his purchase becomes effective if the principal ratifies

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The buyer always keeps the slave
B) So-and-so takes the slave unless he denies ordering the purchase
C) The seller keeps the slave
D) The slave goes to the state

Key Takeaway
The buyer's iqrar of agency is binding and only the principal's denial can repudiate it; sale by ta'ati is valid based on custom and mutual consent.

Agency to Buy Two Specified Slaves: Price Limits and Binding Effect
Ruling on buying one or both specified slaves with or without price specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules on permissible price deviation in agency for purchase and determine when the principal is bound by the agent's purchase of one or both specified items.

Core Idea
An agent for purchase may buy at fair value or with slight overcharge; gross overcharge invalidates. If total price is specified for equal items, half each is implied.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies two key scenarios in agency (wakāla) for purchase of specified slaves. First, when no price is fixed, the agent must avoid gross overpricing (ghaban fāḥish). Second, when a total price is named for two equally valuable slaves, the price is apportioned equally by implication, so buying one at half or less is a deviation to the principal's benefit and binds him, while buying at more is detrimental and does not bind.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
The passage first discusses absolute agency (no price restriction), then agency with a total price specified for two specific slaves. Recognize which scenario applies.
2
Identify the permissible price range in absolute agency
An agent for purchase may buy at the item's true value or with a slight overcharge (ghaban yasīr). Gross overcharge (ghaban fāḥish) invalidates the purchase by consensus – this is unique to agency for purchase, not sale.
Contrast with agent for sale who may sell at any price per Abu Hanifah.
3
Analyze the specified total price scenario
If the principal orders: 'Buy these two slaves for 1000' and their values are equal, the command implies 500 per slave by linguistic necessity (dilāla). Buying one at 500 is exact compliance; below 500 is a deviation to benefit; above 500 is a deviation to detriment.
The rule applies only when values are equal; if unequal, different rules apply.
4
Apply the deviation principle (mukhālafa ilā khair/sharr)
A deviation to benefit (buying for less) is valid and binds the principal. A deviation to detriment (buying for more) is not binding on the principal; the agent bears liability if he used his own funds.
The purchase itself is valid (ṣaḥīḥ), but the principal may reject it.
5
Determine the ruling for each purchase
State clearly: if the agent buys one slave for ≤500, the purchase binds the principal. If >500, the purchase is valid but the principal is not bound; the agent is liable.
This is the muftā bihī position from Abu Hanifah.

وعينين: أي معينين فلو غير معينين بطل التوكيل. (ط) فاشترى له أي بقدر قيمته أو بزيادة يتغابن الناس فيها، وما لا يتغابن فيه فلا يجوز إجماعا؛ لأنه توكيل بالشراء، وهو لا يحتمل الغبن الفاحش بخلاف الوكيل بالبيع عند الإمام، فإنه يبيع ما قل وكثر على ما يجئ، وقوله: "صح" أي الشراء؛ لأن التوكيل مطلق عن قيد شرائهما متفرقين أو مجتمعين، فيجري على إطلاقه، وغير مقيد بثمن مقدر، فيجوز أن يشتري له كل واحد منهما بقدر قيمته أو بغبن يسير، ويقع هذا الشراء على الموكل؛ لأنه لم يخالف في الإتيان بما أمر به. (عيني، فتح) صح: أي ولو أمره بشراء عبدين معينين. (عيني) وبشرائهما بألف إلخ [ أي الشراء للآمر؛ لأن التوكيل مطلق غير مقيد بثمن مقدر. (عيني)] أي لو أمره أن يشتريهما بألف وقيمتهما سواء، فعند أبي حنيفة: إن اشترى أحدهما بخمس مائة أو أقل، جاز، ويقع للآمر ؛ لأنه قابل الألف بالعبدين، وقيمتهما سواء، فتنقسم عليهما نصفين دلالة، فيكون أمراً بشراء كل واحد منهما بخمس مائة ضرورة، فالشراء بخمس مائة موافقة، وبأقل منها مخالفة إلى خير، وقوله: "وبالأكثر" أي لا فلا يلزم الموكل؛ لأن الشراء بالزيادة مخالفة إلى شر قليلة كانت أو كثيرة، يصح،
And 'two specified slaves': meaning specific; if they were unspecified, the agency would be invalid. (T) So he bought for him, meaning at the value or with an increase that people usually tolerate (yutaghāban), and what is not tolerated is not allowed by consensus; because it is an agency for purchase, which does not tolerate gross overpricing (ghaban fāḥish), unlike the agent for sale according to Imam [Abu Hanifah], who may sell for little or much as will come. And his statement: 'valid' meaning the purchase; because the agency is absolute, not restricted by the condition of buying them separately or together, so it runs on its absolute nature, and not restricted by a specified price. So he may buy each one of them at its value or with a slight overpricing (ghaban yasīr), and this purchase is valid for the principal; because he did not deviate from what he was ordered. (Ayni, Fath) 'Valid': meaning even if he ordered him to buy two specific slaves. (Ayni) 'And with their purchase for a thousand, etc.' [meaning the purchase is for the principal; because the agency is absolute, not restricted by a specified price. (Ayni)] Meaning: if he ordered him to buy them for a thousand while their values are equal, then according to Abu Hanifah: if he bought one of them for five hundred or less, it is valid and falls for the principal; because he assessed the thousand against the two slaves, and their values are equal, so it divides between them by implication into halves, so the order is necessarily to buy each for five hundred. So buying for five hundred is compliance, and for less is a deviation to good (khilāf ilā khair). And his statement: 'and with more' meaning no, then it does not bind the principal; because buying for more is a deviation to bad (khilāf ilā sharr), whether little or much, [the purchase] is valid (on the agent).
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage covers two sub-rules within the chapter of agency for purchase. First: if a principal appoints an agent to buy two specific slaves without naming a price, the agent may buy each at its fair market value or with a slight overcharge (ghaban yasir). Gross overcharging invalidates the purchase by consensus because agency for purchase does not tolerate flagrant exploitation. This differs from an agent for sale, who according to Imam Abu Hanifah can sell at any price. Second: if the principal specifies a total price (e.g., 1000) for two slaves of equal value, the agent may buy one for half or less, and it binds the principal because the principal's order implied half each. Buying one for more than half is a deviation to the agent's disadvantage (khilaf ila sharr), does not bind the principal, and the agent would be liable.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghaban al-fāḥish): Gross overpricing that is not tolerated in agency for purchase; such purchase is invalid by consensus
التوكيل المطلق (al-tawkil al-muṭlaq): Absolute agency without restriction on price or method
مخالفة إلى خير / إلى شر (mukhālafa ilā khair / ilā sharr): Deviation from the principal's order that is to the principal's benefit (buying for less) vs. to his detriment (buying for more)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the agent buys one of two equally-valued slaves for 600 when the principal ordered both for 1000?
A) The purchase is valid and binds the principal
B) The purchase is invalid
C) The purchase does not bind the principal; the agent is liable for the extra
D) The principal has the option to accept or reject

Key Takeaway
In agency for purchase, beneficial deviations bind the principal; detrimental deviations do not. When a total price is specified for equal items, half per item is implied.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Agency to Purchase Specified Slaves: Price and Equality Issues
Rulings on purchasing specified slaves without price and with a lump sum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent purchasing one of two specified slaves for more than half the lump sum, and apply the istihsan exception.

Core Idea
Purchasing one of two slaves for more than half is a violation, but istihsan may validate it if the second is purchased.

When a principal orders an agent to purchase two specified slaves for a lump sum, the agent must not exceed the implied equal division. But human transactions are messy. What if the agent buys one at a higher price? The Hanafi school, through Abu Hanifa, provides a nuanced ruling that balances contractual fidelity with the principal's ultimate goal. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the intra-madhhab dispute with the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's order
The principal orders the agent to purchase two specified slaves (e.g., Zayd and Amr) for a lump sum (e.g., 1000 dirhams). Their values are equal. What is the implied division?
The text says 'values are equal' so by indication each is worth half.
2
Analyze the agent's action
The agent purchases one slave for more than half (e.g., 600 for a 500-value slave). Is this a violation? According to Abu Hanifa, yes, because the principal's order implied 500 per slave.
The violation is a 'mukhalafa ila sharr' (violation to bad).
3
Apply Abu Hanifa's default rule
The purchase of the first slave at 600 is not binding on the principal. It is valid but not effective unless salvaged by istihsan.
The text says 'la yalzam al-muwakkil' (does not bind the principal).
4
Apply the istihsan exception
If the agent subsequently purchases the second slave with the remaining 400 before any litigation, the first purchase becomes binding. The principal's purpose (owning both) is achieved, so the indication of equal division falls away.
Istihsan overrides the strict qiyas that would invalidate the first purchase.
5
Compare with Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn hold that the first purchase at 600 is valid immediately as long as the increase is not gross (ghubn fahish) and the remainder suffices for the other. Their reasoning focuses on the principal's goal, not the implied division.
The practical difference: under Sahibayn, no need to wait for the second purchase; the first is binding from the start.

Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage covers several sub-rulings within the chapter of agency for sale and purchase. First, it discusses the case where a principal orders an agent to purchase two specified slaves ('aynayn) without naming a price. The agent purchases one of them. The ruling: the purchase is valid and falls on the principal, as long as the price is not grossly excessive (ghubn fahish). The agent may purchase at a price equal to the value or with a slight increase that people overlook. The authority for this is that the agency is absolute, not restricted to purchasing both together or separately, and not restricted to a fixed price. Therefore, purchasing one at a fair price is compliance. Second, if the principal orders the agent to purchase both slaves for a thousand dirhams and their values are equal, then Abu Hanifa rules: if the agent purchases one for five hundred or less, it is valid; if he purchases one for more than five hundred (even slightly), it is not binding on the principal unless he also purchases the remaining slave with the balance before any dispute arises. The reasoning is that when the principal says 'buy both for a thousand,' and their values are equal, the thousand is implied to be divided equally, so each slave is effectively priced at five hundred. Purchasing one at more than five hundred is a violation. However, by istihsan, if the agent later purchases the second slave for the remaining balance, the principal's purpose is achieved and the first purchase becomes binding. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) differ: they allow purchasing one for more than half if the increase is slight (what people overlook) and the balance suffices for the other, because the goal is to own both. Abu Hanifa's view is based on the implied equal division. Third, the passage discusses a creditor ordering his debtor to purchase a specific slave with the debt. The purchase is valid on the creditor (principal), and the slave is considered the creditor's property even if it dies before delivery. The debtor is merely an agent. Fourth, if the order is to purchase an unspecified slave, then Abu Hanifa rules the purchase is effective on the agent (not the principal) because the agency is void due to uncertainty (the principal did not specify the seller or the item). However, if the principal takes possession, it becomes his. The two (Sahibayn) hold it binding on the principal. The principle is that agency with a debt is only valid if the seller or the item is specified; otherwise, it is void.

Key Terms
الغبن الفاحش (al-ghubn al-fahish): Gross negligence or excessive overpricing that is not overlooked in transactions.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if an agent is ordered to purchase two slaves of equal value for 1000 dirhams, and he purchases one for 600 dirhams, what is the status of that purchase?
A) It is valid and binding on the principal immediately.
B) It is invalid and not binding on the principal at all.
C) It is not binding on the principal unless he also purchases the other slave with the remaining 400 dirhams before any dispute.
D) It is valid only if the principal ratifies it.

Key Takeaway
Purchasing one of two slaves for more than half the lump sum is a violation, but can be cured by purchasing the second with the balance before dispute, based on istihsan.
